O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, dear son, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine along with its fulfillment, and I made the end through its expositions and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of the hands, namely surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of the hands is neglected in our region and is foreign to all, the science has been lost and severed, and nothing remains of its force except for small descriptions in books by the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed off and science is kept at a distance.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	I think I want to animate it together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and will come together with the forms of cautery tools and other instruments of the work, along with the adjustment of their declaration and preparation as needed.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of the hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And one who undertakes this should excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, as far as he knows the judgment of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and the moving and resting places of them, and where their channels originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this reason, Hypocras says that the name with the name is much, but with the work is little.
et meismement en l’art de main.	and especially in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not aware of the things previously mentioned, should be careful that he does not fall into error and harm people;
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	so that I have often encountered many of those who meddle in this science and abandon themselves without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish surgeon who lanced an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and he lanced the arteries in the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	because so much blood flows out that the woman dies between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone in a man's urinary tract; and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	carried with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and if they cut it out he would certainly die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another surgeon who treated the Duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was an injury;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the ignorant surgeons pulled on the break above the wound so hard that they dislocated it, and did not leave any padding on the wound, and left him like this with an open wound;
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and commanded that he should not reset it;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and he remained like this with his leg swollen and the foot, and he came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and hurried to come and reset the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I dislocated it, it was put at ease and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	However, the corruption had already settled in the limb, and he could not heal it;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not cease from spreading through the limb until all of the limb was destroyed.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another case where a doctor lanced an abscess that was swollen, and then it became inflamed due to the maliciousness of his lord.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because when a ulcer is free of melancholy humor, it must not be touched with iron unless in such a place that one can completely remove all that which is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for this reason, very dear son, you need to know that the work of medicine is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is, work where there is danger in many conditions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	So it is necessary that you be careful, so that foolish people cannot speak badly of you.Car li savans ommes qui sont en art traittanz, por ses consillanz qu’ilz donnt, doivent être mesurs en chescun le
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	So take up your weapons in this way, and approach your illnesses lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you will achieve salvation and be praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and let the dreadful illnesses of deep sorrow
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and set aside your arms from that which causes you to doubt, and have faith in yourselves so that you may pass from this world into the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen says in some of his warnings:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take on a difficult disease unless you are called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and hot iron cauteries, and it covers the head down to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and includes the forms of instruments, and the tools for cautery, and all that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and includes leeches, wounds, extracting arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and it covers the tools and their forms.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twisting, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it covers the head down to the feet, and includes the tools' forms.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus, as we remember the work, it is fitting that I say something about the nature of each temperament and their harmful effects.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of medicine, and understanding illness, are the most lengthy speech and subtle knowledge, and the secrets of remedies;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and of this spoke many of the sages, and agreed upon it;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and I am content with little of their words, for I fear length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery aids universally in every complexion where it has matter, except in two complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	that is to know hot complexion without matter, and dry complexion without matter.En la complexion chaude sens matiere, il n’a point de matere, si qu’il ne peuit cauterier:
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In hot and dry complexion with matter together, some people have spoken and said that cautery is of great aid;Car li feu s’en va sur la matere et le corps reste en repos;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and others said the opposite:Car li feu s’en va sur la matiere et ne touche
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	Because fire goes into the matter and does not touch the body;And they say that cautery is worth nothing for illnesses that come from heat and dryness.Mais en la complexeion flege
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	But in the phlegmatic complexiona the nature of fire is hot, and should not be treated with heat for hot illnesses, nor for dryness;Et en la complexeion sanguine, car li feu ne se doit mie adrezier a la maladious qui vient de sang, car il est de nature cha
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and those who say the contrary, that cautery does great good for hot and dry diseases that come upon men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found this to be true through experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	Nevertheless, one should not employ it except for those who have experienced it and who know through long practice the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of men's complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and their outcomes and the season of the year.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	Of other complexions we have no fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors agreed and concurred about the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my son, that cautery combines fire with the secrets of cures, and is of greater goodness than burning cautery of medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not spread to any other part of the body apart from where it is applied, and it does no harm if properly used.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Burning medicines move from one member to another, causing grief and poor healing in the member.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	And by chance they may kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its height and the goodness of its substance, does not do this unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And that I have found through experience and through the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and been in the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and because of this I excuse myself for the length of my speech, for I do not wish to take away from you the secret that is hidden in fire, and the nature of its work, how it drives out illnesses of the body, as the philosopher explains in his demonstration.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time cauteries should be performed, and chose a favorable moment.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harmful humors are driven out by the help of cautery.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And especially if the cautery is for painful and urgent conditions that cannot wait until a later time when greater harm might come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think, dear son, as fools do,
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	because the illness that is healed by cautery does not return;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say it thus:
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they believe; for cautery is only a medicine that moves the complexions and dries the humors which are the cause of the pain; it is worth more than other medicines because of its swiftness, its virtue, and its lordship.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible for a disease to come sometimes according to the complexion of the patient, and the location of the disease, and its virtue.
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and the excesses are gathered in him through the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauterization is administered to where he has little excess and moisture, as with dental cauterizations for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and that is evident;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauterization comes after medicine, but their intentions are false, and cauterization is the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment in any disease and they do not work, then we turn to cauterization, and it does work.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is clear that cauteries are indeed the last resort of medicine, not according to the understanding of foolish people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cauteries made of gold instruments are better than those of iron, and they only said this because of the quality of gold and because of the height of its substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and said that the heat of the cautery does not make blisters, but this is not true, for I have tested it and found that it is true in some people.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and gold cauteries are better than those of iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And yet, when you heat up a gold instrument, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools down immediately;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if it is heated too much,
si font au feu;	if they are heated in fire,
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and so there are enough obstacles.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use fire cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Here I have arranged this chapter from the head to the feet so that the way is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and coldness on the head, and there are two types of disease caused by it, one called "soda", and by many humors which descend from the head to the eyes, and ears, and also from many diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with purifying medicine for three or four nights, depending on what the nature and age of the disease can tolerate;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	And then have the patient's head examined.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on his knees;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	Afterwards, place the palm of your hand between his eyebrows, between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then bring your two middle fingers down, and let it bleed then heat the cautery called "olive", of which this is the shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and move your hand up and down while squeezing it gently;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then lift your hand slightly, and examine the spot if you see the bone under the skin;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	And if you do not see it, reheat the cautery as I have instructed you until you see the bone;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	Afterwards, take a piece of silk and place some soft cotton inside it and tie it up, and place it on the spot and leave it for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	after moistened with cotton in butter;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave it until the burn is healed;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards, treat the wound with an ointment called 'tetrafarmaçon' until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And they say that when the wound is left open for longer, it drains more effectively;
et por ce si aide mues.	and because of this, pus is expelled.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some say that one should let the cautery burn so much that part of the bone is burned, and then have what is burned of the bone resected and then cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And some say that one should leave the cautery on for so long, and press down so hard that it cuts through the bone as widely as the ring that women put on their fingers to draw out humours;
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must keep the wound open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	afterwards, one should treat and bandage it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me at all, except in some people where there is a fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and I think I should let him go;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the head is weakened by the continuous secretions of nature, as we witness in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and likewise when the head is weakened by illness and the first appearance of cautery is gentler for me, I therefore work towards a joint salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When there is chronic pain throughout the head, lasting a long time, one should use herbs and pills for illness, and purgatives for the head, as well as oils and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one performs the cautery that we mentioned earlier and it does not help,
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care that the head of the ill person is not of a hot nature, and that it is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize him under that cautery which we mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After that, do cauterization on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and do cauterization in the place which is called "vessels".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and there are places where one puts leeches;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and lighten your hand so that you do not go up to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and the cauteries on the horns should be thinner than those used to cauterize the middle of the head, and that is the form;Aprés ke li cauteres soit fitz sus les cornes,
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery of the head:
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	After that, when sudden pain arises in a part of the head, and the disease is spread to the eye, and the shoulder is purged by purifying medicines, and all the other remedies I have described in the division of diseases, and none of them help:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then make cauteries according to two methods, namely of medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cautery of medicine is that you take a piece of alder, remove the bark and wrap it around both shoulders, and then make the sign of the cross on the skin where the pain is, in such a way that you can place the piece of alder underneath the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	And when it is placed, tie it and hold it tightly and leave it for twelve hours.
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	Then untie it and pull it away from the alder, and leave the wound like that for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	Then place a long piece of cotton soaked in butter over the wound until it heals.IIe cautere de feir est que tu prendes une fumee de chanvre, et le fent bruleer
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	The cautery of fire is that you take hemp smoke and burn itAfter the wound has healed, treat the scar with ointment until it is gone.and then the patient should
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see fit to use some of the burning medicines that I have written about in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done in this way.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery tool until it is the right temperature.
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called a "cleft" because the head is formed in the shape of a cleft or pit, and in the middle has a small protrusion;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it over the painful area, and hold your hand and gently turn the fire a little bit, so that half of the thickness of the skin is burned;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and quickly take your hand away so that the artery does not burn and flow profusely with blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Afterwards, put cotton wool soaked in vinegar on it, and keep it there for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply wet cotton wool with butter, and then heal the area with ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you wish to cauterize this hemorrhoid with the cautery called "culterium", do so at the very tip only, and be careful not to touch the artery in this hemorrhoid which is not old.
de emigraine	of hematoma
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a migraine as we have previously described in the sections on diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the cautery previously mentioned in the medicine section and the fire do not help, then you must heat the cautery tool called "cultellare" until it turns white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	And you sign the area over the vein with a line of about half an inch in length, and move your hand away once, and press it so that you do not cover the artery and go all the way to the bone.
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	And beware of the jaw that mutes when one chews, and the nerve should not be affected so that there is no muteness or spasm in the patient, and beware of blood flow from the artery when it is cut, for this can cause great fear both to the unskilled and inexperienced person.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leave the work halfway done;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it opens in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery is not sufficient for the disease and the patient is suffering, cauterize him in the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	And if you see that he needs the cautery we mentioned in the chapter on extraction of the artery, with the cautery tool that has two knives;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this cautery is better and more effective than the other one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	from pain in the ears due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ear from cold, and one has applied dissolving medicines and other treatments that we have described in the division, and the pain does not go away, then heat this cautery, which is called a «point», with which there is a needle at its end:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After you have marked the area around the ear where the pain is located in both ears, or in one if it is only there, and then move slightly up from the root of the ear, where you will make the incision;
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and has six points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treating the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Wounds that must be treated with cautery are only those that cause pus, as we have said in the sections on diseases;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not use cautery on sores that come from dryness and nerve pain.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this type of wound that discharges fluid from the ears and nose, and cleaning the head and gargling do not help, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, another a little above the temple, and the third in the junction between the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery in the part that appears healthy, and cauterize above the head of the ear, a little below the horn of the head, and another one on the temple as long as a finger;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery on until the middle of the heart is burned;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And the appearance of the tweezers that we have put before, but it is a bit more subtle and the tweezers should be a bit thicker;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	after cleaning the area as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is old and you treat it thus as we have said, and it does not help, and the patient has a fever, then make 4 cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	2 on the 2 horns of the head, and 1 in the middle of the head, and 1 in the place called "vessel", as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	of litharge
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this disease, give the patient large pills that cleanse the brain.
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	After washing the head of the patient thoroughly, place a mustard plaster described in the chapter on plasters upon his forehead.
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	And this is how to do the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if he does it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is healed like this, it is good.Si li peilz sont lons et igals, et s’il ne le point
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	And if the hairs are long and even, and if he does not feel any pricking, make three cauteries on his head, going from above to below, and space them two fingers apart.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	And treat it as the others, and if you see any swelling, and the patient can endure it, make a cautery in the middle.et s’il ne le peut demorer ains qu’il se mueve ou se desaluit, tu le remets a leu; et se li estraint les eulz, li fai III
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if necessary, two others on the two horns, and cure it until it is healed;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and use the cautery called "olive", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of cold from the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	The head should be cleansed of hair and of what we mentioned earlier;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	after resetting the dislocated head, then cauterize in the head and on each horn, and once behind and three times on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is severe, then do three cauteries on the spine of the back;et si tu veiles le fere sanz douleur et sanz grant lesion, covient que li cauteres soit ben fitz et frids.
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and leave it until the most sensitive part is burned and lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	then cure it until it is healed, and use the cautery called "olive" as we mentioned earlier.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first cleanse the brain of hair and other remedies that we have mentioned in the division when the disease is great and suffering from taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot bear it, make him gargle and chew, purifying the brain often with good meat;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	after the king comes the head in the middle, and do the cautery according to what we have said before, and the cautery on the vessel, and on each horn;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the disease is external and bearable, do cauteries as I have said for someone with paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olive according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the disease is in an infant, make a small cautery according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When through the cause of melancholy there are corrupted humours and thick phlegm, then cauterize with mild cauteries as we have said for paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if through the cause of melancholy the humours are inclined towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give them something to drink that will cleanse the brain, according to what is said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After the king comes the head of the disease;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	Then make a well-made linen bandage, like a circle, and place it on the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and let the disease be crossed, and be well held from all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	Then offer the linen, and put on a poultice of old goat's butter;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and the hot cautery temperately, so that he can bear it;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	after emptying the ring from within the head, and leaving it to cool;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this to the patient once a week with other good treatment, until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or, if you wish to cauterize the eye, make several small points on the entire cautery tool.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This cautery method moistens the brain greatly;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put wet cotton in mutton tallow and grease of goose.
de l’awe des eulz	of their eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When awfulness first comes to the eyes through the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient drink that cleanses the head, and guard it from all moisture, and make him sweat in a bath several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	Afterwards he has his head shaved and cauterized in the head, and he does two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of the eye is to both eyes together, or one if it is to one;
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and cover all the veins and arteries that are under the skin, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and beware of bleeding, and if you see too much blood issuing, stop it as best you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and the incision, the cautery how you should apply it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and sometimes a cautery or hatchet is made under the two bones at the back.
dou cors des larmes	where the body weeps
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears are old and habitual and on top of the veins, or alongside the arteries that are visible on the outside of the head;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and it can be seen that they are cold phlegmatic superfluities, then he should make the cautery which I described earlier, descending towards the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I cautery on the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or hatchets under the two bones;
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if there is more need, then he should cauterize bleeding above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	from the body through the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you treat him according to what we have described in the division, and it does not help, then give the patient three nights of cow's milk;
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	after the king, the head, and the cautery with olive oil.
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make the cauteries called "clavicles" over the two joints, a little under the hair.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and be careful of the artery that you do not cover it up.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the film of the eye becomes soft due to illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery tool called "olive".Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste maniere.
de coi ci est li forme:	The fire cautery is done in this way.
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see to make two cauteries over the two joints as long as the joints are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not leave the hand there except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to what I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes the hair in the armpits turns inward and pricks the underarm, and cauteries are done according to two methods; one is:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is, with fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	The fire cautery instructs the patient to let the hair grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they grow long and even, then put the cautery to the patient's skin.
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	Afterwards, draw on paper a figure that is also like the hollow of the myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be between the hairs.
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then place cotton soaked in egg white and sweet alyssum musk on the eye; then heat the cautery with which this figure is formed.
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	Afterwards, cauterize over the figure that you have drawn a little bit at a time many times so that the heat burns the area.
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	And the sign of the treatment's success is when you see the skin raised and the hairs standing upright at the edge of the eye.
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then loosen your hand, and let it be for three days, then place wet cotton in the buttocks until the scald is healed.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the wound has healed, treat it with ointment until it is healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if afterwards the hairs grow, and the skin becomes soft, then restart the cautery on the same spot, just as you did before;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs fall out, then cauterize it until the skin returns to its natural state, and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The burning cautery of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take French soap and live charcoal, of each one-third, and grind them well together;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and make it quickly so that it does not cool, then spread over the shape you have made like a myrtle leaf, and place some on the paper;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the disease is in one eye only, then one must treat that one, and if in both, then both;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and place under the eye moist cotton soaked in egg white;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and let the head of the patient be in a healthy position and place your hand showing the medicine, and press it hard and move it all the time that the patient feels biting from the medicine, for he will feel biting as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your body.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the biting has passed, lift up the eyelid, and look to see if the paper is also lifted up as it was by the constraint of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if so, then all is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, then continue with the medication on the area until the work is equalized and the eyes are put in place.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put wet cotton on the burns until they heal, and then treat the area of the ointment that is called "diaper" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to be careful with your work, so that it does not break the medicine on them.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterward, and the hair pricks in the eye, then continue the medication on that area which is softened by the paper properly, just as you did before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the shape of the bellows:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that men's eyes are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this, the constraints should be;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and the right way is not revealed to those who have dedicated themselves to this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	on the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you are treating a fistula as we have described in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then you must perform cautery on it according to this manner. Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head in your lap.
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold his head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or drop.
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	After that, place wet cotton in the white of an egg or in juice of parsley on his eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	afterwards heat the cautery which is made thus:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and shaped like a quill pen on one end, and on the other end is the cautery;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you want it pointed at both ends, or if you want it also shaped like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but that which is shaped like a quill pen is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	Afterwards press the fistula if it is open and draw out the pus and dry it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, then open it and draw out the fluid;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	Afterward, put on the hot cautery, and hold your hand to the cautery at the part under the eye, so that your hand does not make foolishness.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery right up to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then renew the cautery again once more, and if you need another one, leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	Afterward, put on wet cotton in butter, and let it be cured by the dry ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then use corrosive medicine until the bone is uncovered;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and treat it according to how it comes in his eye.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula which some of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Pay attention to a fistula, and probe the site;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Afterward, put in the slit one small needle so that it is at the base:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and make it the size of an egg;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand over the cautery firmly, and do not move the patient until the plaster has set;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and you should put wet cotton on the patient's eye, soaked in vinegar or wine:
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the plaster will heal the fistula miraculously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization that we have described, then it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, one must administer an incision to the nail, and bring the fistula back into the body of the nail according to what is appropriate in its own place.And if the cauterization does not heal the fistula, then you should make an incision on the nail, and bring the fistula back into the body of the nail according to where it belongs.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there are cracks in the lips which are called "hairs," and especially so in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have described above in sections, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small blade-like cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And it will gradually heal those fissures until they are closed;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the area with ointment until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess forms at the root of the gum, or in the uvula, or palate, or tooth roots, and there is swelling and pus and it becomes a fistula:
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have described in the section on incisions, but it does not help:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then you must have the cautery according to the size of the fistula.
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand steady so that the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and then go around it from behind.
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this once or twice after the treatment we have described for fistulas, until it is healed.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is treated thus, that is good.
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, then you must expose the area and remove the rotten bone, according to what you find in his shoulder.
dou movement des dens	the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but it doesn't help, then put the head of the patient in your lap.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after heating the cautery whose shape will be described below, you apply it to the tooth by placing a piece of cotton on it.
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and place the hot cautery gently within, and hold your hand steady so that the patient feels the heat reach the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	then remove your hand and repeat with the cautery as desired.
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	afterwards, fill the patient's mouth with salt water and let it sit for an hour and release the forces.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner, the tooth that was loose is now firmly fixed, and the gums are softened and restrained, and the putrid moisture is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When tooth pain comes from coldness, or there is coldness or whiteness, and the remedies of medicine are ineffective, then cautery is needed in two ways:Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cautery with butter and fire cautery.For fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Butter cautery: take butter from a cow, and its end in a spoon made of iron or bronze;Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des sai
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	take cotton and wrap it around the end of a tent-peg, soak it in buttock's milk, and apply it to the aching tooth until it is relieved.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and do this often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth. And if you see it moistened wool and cotton in cold buttock's milk, and put on the aching tooth, and put on the hot iron until the fire comes to the gum of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cautery together is such that you take an iron or bronze rod, and let it be thick so that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	Afterwards heat the cautery, of which the shape will come later, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be removed that day or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And the patient must fill his mouth with good butter quickly before this cautery, and then let it cool down.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And this is how to make the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And take any part of the body you want, according to what you are able;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	And this is how to make the cauterizing iron:
des scrophules	of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When scrofula is cold and moist, and not subject to digestion by medicine, then heat the cauterizing iron so that it becomes very hot, and let the smoke come out of the iron from one side to the other;
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	And place the hot cauterizing iron on the abscess once, or as many times as necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	And if the abscess is small, apply the cauterizing iron according to the size of the abscess, and leave it for three days.
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and apply moist cotton to the burn until the scald is removed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	thereafter, treat the site with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moisture prevails over the channels of the lungs, and particularly when it comes from a cold constitution, then the patient should first be purged with medicine that dissolves.
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	After that, he should have cautery at the root of his throat; and be careful not to go any higher than the throat, but only burn a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After that, he should have another cautery at the junction of neck and head, at the top of the spine, and it should be a cautery called 'clavicle' as we have described earlier;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the site as we have said before until it is healed.Appré le fai I cautere sus la jointure de leus coudies, et apret les teneures qui li
de la toust	of the tongue
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all diseases of the chest are from cold moistors, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and is an old disease if he .II cauteries on the breast in their homes;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery between the breasts between II;

et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the points be to XXX, or around.Et soit l’espas de li poins XX a la cote selonc la granture del mal;
