Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make it with a cane of bronze or iron according to this form, and let it be thin underneath and drawn out on top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	Do not pierce it, lest it remain in the body, and press hard.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you want to cauterize the numbness, as it is done before in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	One makes a clyster from silver or gold, or from melted and hammered copper;
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and sometimes they are made small or large according to those who receive them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are administered to children, the weak and sick, should be small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the enema, whether it is small or large, depends on the width of the rectum, according to this method:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	And one makes an incision on the abdomen, as you see, and the intestines are pierced inside;
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and there is one hole on each side;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and the abdomen where the medicine is placed is made from a beast's bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and there should be one finger width between each hole, then insert into these holes a strong thread twisted in an X shape or spiral around, and assemble the abdomen as if it were a goat;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread in front, then clysterize;
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And its shape is circular:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And the medicine should not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the tip of the syringe with oil or egg white, or similar, then insert it gently;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	Then the assistant squeezes the bulb with both hands simultaneously until it is empty, then withdraws the syringe and lets the patient straighten his legs, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him strain as much as he can;
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And if he sleeps for a night afterwards, it is of greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use the syringe for the sickness of a flowing stomach, and the medicine rushes out, he should repeat it until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are internal or an abscess, then the syringe should be as thin as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And its shape is slender where the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already said in the section on wound treatment:
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	And you shall tell of the cures of hands and of medicine, according to what is accomplished.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the place where the wounds are made, and what makes them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by splitting of stone, and cutting with sword and knife, or spear or staff or arrow, or similar objects;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or according to the locations in the body, such as a wound that falls upon the neck, or head, or thigh, or belly, or liver, and similar organs;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds in the head, for the memory will come to me as I go.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, then take care whether it is from splitting of stone or similar objects, and the skin is still broken and the wound is large, and you fear quickly an abscess of heat:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if he immediately bleeding from the cephalic vein if it comes little blood from the wound, and let the bleeding be in the opposite direction of the damaged part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and prevent the patient from eating wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to bleed, let his food be diminished, and do not drink wine or eat meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put cotton moistened only in rose oil or wine on the wound if hot abscesses come out;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, put on the wound, which must be fresh with all its blood, and not moved by air, powder, which I will describe a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the air has moved it, put some ointments on it until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a sword, and the lips cannot be brought together by sutures, then bring them together by stitches, as I will describe for wounds in the abdomen, in the rib cage.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and can be sewn up, and it holds except for a little bit, then sew it up;
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then heal the wound with medicine, and restore firm flesh in place of the skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as testicles and cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find pus in the skin, and it does not reach the bone, then scrape off all of the pus, and pour it out, then heal it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which causes bleeding, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then bind it with a thread;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is easy:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and you should put on this powder that heals as soon as the fire has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the way of making the powder is as follows:
pren encens une partie;	take incense one part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	fine chalk three parts, and powdered very finely, and apply the powder to the wound, and hold it firmly, until it clings well and draws out all the blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	then bind it up tightly, and leave it loose if it swells;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one does not remove the medicine until the wound is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes cautery is done with a hot iron only, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood; but the wound must be moved by the cautery.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the burn has moved the wound, do the same, but don't apply any of this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but rather apply some digestive ointments, or barley flour made with water and honey, until the swelling goes down;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if there is a broken bone with the wound, and it is small, then hold it with fine pins;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about fractures of the head afterward.
de la plaie dou col	of a wound on the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is in the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's a nerve, there should be nothing done but to leave the wound alone and not put anything constricting on it, because it hurts the nerves and makes them withdraw.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And nothing cold should be placed on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	But the medicine should be warm, like chamomile washed in warm water and mixed with rose oil, and cooked wash also in warm water, and other herbs of similar nature, and moist poultices.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cut it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and she has a hernia and is full of bowels, then cut her open higher up or lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if an artery is cut and bleeding results, then ligate it, and let it be cut out, and cauterized if necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the airway is kept clear so that the meat can pass through, then press on the windpipe above the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then gently tighten it, and leave it for a few days, then treat it with cleansing ointments until it is healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then fill it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are bone fragments, then remove them all as much as you can, and those that you cannot reach, leave them until the wound heals, and the bloodletting is complete;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder it with the powder I have described.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have described in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a spear or knife wound, and the wound is deep, then examine if from the wound any bad air escapes:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	Know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put any powder on it in the first hour, nor tie it for the blood to stop pouring out, but let it return to the body and heal the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you do not have an ointment, put old cotton in the wound to draw out moisture and let the patient sleep on the wound for three days or four or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	and if no spasms come, nor trembling of the heart, nor pain in the joints;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see these good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal it then with poultices and other remedies until it is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal and work, then you know there is a fistula.
si la cure si com on doit.	treat the wound as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a cut by a sword or knife, and it is simple, on the front or back, then treat it as follows:
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, stitch it up.
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, treat it with powder, and if it has cut into the bone, and broken off pieces, then clean the wound, and draw out the foreign bodies if they are lodged in there.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if they are not lodged, let the wound fester so that it will expel the foreign bodies.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	For other wounds on other limbs, the treatment is as we have already said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	There are many types of stomach ruptures: large, medium and small.Li grans est quan li corps del veine est rompu, ou quan li membre est desveu de
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of a great wound except sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, through which the entrance of air;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because one returns the intestines to it more often with pins, if one does not return them little by little from warm to cold;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines swell as soon as they feel cold, so they return more often with pins, and that is why the smaller wound is better, because one resets the intestine to its place earlier than the others Ch.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And you should know that there are IV ways of rupture in the abdomen:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the two common stitches occur in the stomach stitch, and the stitch of other wounds in the body; and two other own stitches are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and nonetheless they are more appropriate with the stomach stitch, and I will say one of them and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and something of the intestine has come out, and a tough thing is difficult to remove, it is by one of two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in such a way:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in lukewarm water only, or cook it in water with squill, cypress, and spike lavender, and warm the intestine until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes make a restraining wine, and apply it alone to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling leaving, moisten the intestine with water or altus and mallows that have been cooked, for through this the entrance is constricted by a little.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is cauterization rather than cutting unless there is a great need for it;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument used to split it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	it should be cut inside the curve and not through, and here is the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines jump out, he puts them back according to their natural shape in their proper place, if you have the power, because it is better that way.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide, and it is on the lower part of the abdomen, then you should make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is on the lower part of the abdomen, then put the head and feet higher than the lower parts, and also if the wound is in one of the sides, then tilt the patient so that the wounded side is higher;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus one must treat both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	For small wounds, take what is appropriate, then hold in your hand the instrument that burns all around the wound, and bring together the edges;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common way of sewing it up, and you must pierce an needle or several, depending on the width of the wound, then leave a gap at the head of the wound, about the thickness of two fingers, and insert an needle there with a strong thread;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two sides of the skin with the two ends of the sinew, which is under the skin inside, so that you make it pierce from that part, and bring together the two ends of the sinew tightly;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then draw a double thread through the needle from both sides, then bring together the two sides of the wound neatly, and then leave another gap, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then make the wound wet with the thread as you did for the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you need of needles, until the entire wound is bound.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be medium-sized, between fine and thick, for the fine needles cut through all the flesh, and the very thick ones cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	because they should be medium-sized.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and one must not push the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, so that they do not cut and open the wound before it is healed.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	then cover the heads of the needles with thread, so that they do not hurt the patient when sleeping, and put tents or rags over the needle-heads to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this way of sewing with needles is best for small wounds, because it requires only one or two needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitch is common, and is where you sew together the two ends of the skin and the two ends of the syringe together with a strong, thin needle;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and once you have pierced all four ends together, bring the needle back to where you started, in the manner that one sews sheets;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave a space between each stitch equal to the thickness of a thumb;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitch healed a man, and I sewed up a wound that a man had on his stomach, which was cut with a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and the intestines protruded over two palms wide, and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned his intestines after they had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was sutured for 15 days, and I healed it, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where one could not find any medicine or treatment;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And put cotton on the wound twice a day, and wash it with honey water until it heals.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	I will tell you two proper methods of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and pierce it through the outside just up to the inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the skin directly, then lay hold of the thread where you put the needle in, and make it pierce through on the other side from inside to out;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the understanding of this stitching is that you sew just as the furriers do with furs, and that you leave the thread once on one side and grab it on the other, so that the stitching is all completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of stitching, which Galen describes properly, is as follows: they assemble the two parts naturally and apply one end of the thread to the other, in such a way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	stick a needle or sharp tool close to the edge, and pierce that spot only, and leave the two sides of the ulcer;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle, and have it pierce from outside to inside, through both sides of the ulcer;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce one and then the other from outside to inside, in two more spots on the edge that are opposite each other;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most common method of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galen says this, and some testify to it: one should stitch the belly with two needles, with thread on both.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should push one needle in from one side and the other from the other, like those who sew wounds;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and know that when the wound is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is more difficult than other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is such that when you probe the fresh wound to its full depth, so that the fire has moved it, then the intestines and the lining are put back into place;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then apply a powder with ointment on top of it while the wound is still open;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and sew up the wound, and close up the edges, and the maw;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as you would any other, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you have no medication, then apply old cotton and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For in most cases where the wounds are simple, you don't need any other medication;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound may affect the principal members, then you should wet a light cloth in warm oil, or rose oil, and place it around the armpits and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if he feels pain or swelling in the bowels, which often happens, then he should be enema with warm black wine, especially if the swelling reaches the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and it should be inserted into them, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine, which is called 'young', cannot heal when it is raw, and this is due to the thinness of the veins that it has, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and its proximity in nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the hernia protrudes from the wound, put it back inside along with the intestine while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and has become black or green, you should tie off the area that is black so that blood does not flow into it, for there are veins and arteries there;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then cut away the tissue between the ligature and place the two ends of the intestine hanging down below the wound until it is easy to extract when the hernia slips out, and close the wound tightly.
de la routure dou boueil	of the road of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are ruptured and the wound is small, it can sometimes be cured in some men, for I saw a man who was pierced through the belly with a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became a fistula, and from it came both excrement and wind;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I knew, and did not cease to apply poultices until he was healed and the wound scars closed over.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw that it was healing, I feared that the patient still had discomfort in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he experienced no ill effects but rather improved in his appetite and digestion;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experiencers say that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be bound in such a way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take a large testicle, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the testicle has opened its mouth, place it upon both lips so that it holds them closed;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cut off his head, and this will be held so that he cannot untie it, then put another noose after in the same way as before, until the wound is completely captured;
et cout la plaie.	and cauterize the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If these worms enter the intestines and cause no harm to the patient, and one can tie off the intestines with a fine thread cut from an animal's intestine in such a way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take the end of this intestine thread that is very charred, and then tie to the end of this thread a fine linen thread wound tightly, then insert the thread into the needle, and cauterize the intestine, and tie it up in the wound;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of sewing up with threads is not foreign to the path of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the small intestines, there is no healing other than through subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it wakes up, is universally called a "fistula", and especially when it is swollen and becomes pus-filled.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the green nodulation of a hardened and white pustule, where one does not feel pain, and it is as smooth as the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it erupts in a clear burst, and sometimes it is thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes it is small, and sometimes larger;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed and there is no scar, it is only due to one of the IX causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the weakness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is a hard scar within, and on the lips, that does not allow a scar to form;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much pus;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the wound is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or medicine does no good in its treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is of a pestilential nature;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the disposition in the region is tardy in digestion, and late in health, and swollen by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones;
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the treatments of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I will tell you about the treatment for a fistula that is done by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula occurs in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for it comes from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, to the face, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the sides, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it occurs in the disposition of the principal member, and in similar ways.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas that are of this manner are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have said, and you have faith in the cure, and you see it, then take a tent of bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, so take it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is crooked, then look for a subtle tent of lead, because lead bends around the crookedness.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well probe it with tents, then cleanse it by enema through one of the openings, because moisture cuts from one opening to another.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	Then probe it with your strength to know if there is bone or nerve, and if the fistula goes deep. Ask the patient about his pain when you press with your hand, and where he feels the pain.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you know truly the location where it is, and whether it is far from joint, nerve, artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have instructed you, and remove the fault and corrupted flesh within.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then treat the wound until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep in a straight place, you should cut it deeply as you can, then put wet bandages soaked in medicine water, and apply them to the head of the fistula so that the medicine corrodes the excess matter remaining at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put healing ointments on healthy flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healed by this method, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If the vein or nerve does not trouble the principal limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, then king's touch as much as the corruption is removed, then the cure of things in infection until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if not healed, and flexed back as before, know that you have not gone to the source:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if uncovered and want to go to the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other way except through cutting;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small corrupt bone, and you can pull it out with tweezers, then remove it with the appropriate instrument for that, and if there are many bones, pull them all out and leave none behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if moisture makes it go against you, and there is no error or fear, then combat the moisture with fire and charcoal, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put something to promote pus on the wound, and let it be around the bones until they become porous, and then they will have the bones more easily;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, like that of the leg or thigh, then treat only the putrefaction until all blackness is removed, and then dress the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large amount of it in the body, and it reaches the bone's marrow;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then it should be cut off and covered all the way to the putrefaction, and then the wound should be treated until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take example and aid from it in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	There was a young man of about 30 years who had pain in his leg caused by an internal issue, so that the matter came out into the leg, and it became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no way to release it by opening it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the doctors, in their folly, worked on it so much that the abscesses opened and discharged a great deal of matter, and became a fistula, and many openings appeared that discharged pus and moisture from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many doctors treated him for 2 years, and there was no improvement in his condition, so that I was called to see him, and I examined his leg and the remedies with which he was being treated, and saw what was flowing from the openings into his body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the young man's body became red, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of the openings, and then I searched all the openings, and found that some came face to face with others throughout the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I quickly examined one of the openings and discovered part of the bone, which was rotten and perforated, and the corruption was spreading to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw what appeared to be a rotted bone, and I thought there was no other corruption than that which I removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	And I began to treat the wound with dry remedies for a long time, but it would not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	And then I began again and exposed the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, which I removed, and then I tried to heal the wound.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	But I could not until I cut around a palm's width of bone, and removed it to the root, then I restored it with remedies.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	And it healed quickly, and there was no need to redo the operation except for the weakness of the patient who could not endure it, and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often the blood evacuated, but it was entirely healed, and in place of the bone a hard lump grew, and it was of good disposition and did not cause any harm or discomfort going or coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if a bone is broken in any part of the body, then one must treat it in this way:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take hold of it, and stretch it to the head of the bone that is exposed, and instruct someone to lift it upward.
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	And place another thicker piece of linen under the first piece, and tie it onto the flesh above the bone, and stretch the head, so that you draw up the corrupted flesh from below, and uncover the flesh above where you see it is, so that the thread does not cut into the flesh.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And place a hot brand or a flat object under the bone to cover up the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And one must sew as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and sew again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, then uncover all the flesh;
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then place a hot brand underneath, and sew from one part of the corruption to the other, with the thread close to the edge of the corruption as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, it corrupts the joint, and on the other side, the bone that contains it;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other remedy but to cut it off;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is in the knuckle of the hand or the foot, it is a very serious matter, but nevertheless you must examine the corrosion and see how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way you can, but be careful that the vein or nerve do not cause any harm;et si tu ne peus pas mondre celle corrosion sans nuire a la veine ne al’artere, mais covient que tu la mundifies par feu ou par caut
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and if you cannot cleanse the corrosion without harming the vein or artery, then you must cleanse it with fire or with cautery. And know that there are many different ways to cut and expose these bones, depending on their placement, appearance, thickness, smoothness, size, and hardness;et si li corruptions est en la veine ou en l’artere, et que li membre soit mort, si doit tu mondre celle veine oultre la corrosion, et le corps mort, selonc la grandece de la veine ou de l’artere, mais non pas plus longement que la veine ou l
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore one must prepare for each type of procedure with their instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work will show you the instrument you need, according to your knowledge of this art and the testimony of the ways of illnesses;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	then guess at the instrument you need based on what it needs.
dou feu	by fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	Shoulders dislocate either due to internal causes or external causes;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have treated that corrosion with medicine and it does not help, then you must cover the affected limb up to where the corrosion is, so that the patient escapes either death or the greater evil of losing the use of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and if there are signs that the limb is turning black and it seems like it has been burned by fire, and after the blackness appears, then the corrosion spreads from limb to limb and affects the whole body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you are bitten, cover the wound immediately, and if it is from the sting of a venomous creature such as a scorpion or serpent, and the bite is on the head or face, then cut off the affected limb and do not give the creature any time to reach your hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches the hand, cut at the joint so that the venom does not travel up the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	And if it reaches the arm, cut at the elbow;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And if it passes the elbow, that is death, and there is no antidote to counter its power save according to its quantity.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	And thus you must act when the sting comes to the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	If it comes to the first joint, cut after the next joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it reaches the foot, cut off the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises up the leg, it will stop at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no cure but to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the method of treating it is to tie the limb above and below, and extend one servant's arm below and another servant's arm above, and you cut the flesh between the two ties with a broad spatula, as far as the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then you stop the bleeding and put a linen cloth on each side so that the wound does not touch the healthy area, and cause him no further injury or abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding occurs when you open it, then cauterize the wound quickly, or put some restraining powders on it.et se li sang ne veult ceurrer, si quieras tu le lames a I piece pour le faire ceurrer, et que li sang vienne en la plaie, si met sus aucune poudres qui s’en
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your medicine until it is complete, then tie the wounded member with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to a man in his sleep;
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	he had a blackness that looked like a burn, and this corrosion came first on his big toe, so much so that it affected the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he immediately covered his foot, and it was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long after, the corrosion returned on his finger, and he came to me, and I applied poultices after cleaning the body, and he could not stop the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I refused, as I had hope of repulsing the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the man's strength was weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he became completely discouraged, returned home, and healed his hand;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not included the stories about what happens if someone else does it, because I don't think we need them.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy part, and remains so long that it causes great swelling;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	then they rupture and drain, and the swelling goes down, and the place where they were is left hollow, like vessels;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin above is as delicate as split silk, and it doesn't adhere to the bone or nerve; such a condition is called "healthy," not a "fistula.
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it becomes so long that it reaches the bone deeply, it is called a  "fistula.
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin such that you cup it all around, especially when it is delicate, just as a napkin.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not tear it for fear of damaging it.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have faith that the skin will heal, and the damage is not complete, and the flesh is thick, then treat it thusly:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	examine if the breasts are swollen, and the belly has a foul odor, then cleanse with an Egyptian medicine made thusly:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take asafoetida, and oil, and litharge, in equal amounts, and mix the ingredients into a vessel over fire, until the medicine turns red and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	then take some according to your need, and dissolve it in water and honey, and cleanse the breast with it, and constrict the nipple;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay on for two hours, then remove it by squeezing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this many times until the breast is deflated and the pain is gone;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and sometimes they are cauterized with water of ashes when this medicine is not present, and it is done by taking ashes from vine wood, pouring water over them, then straining the liquid and using it as a cautery on the breast until you know that the breast is deflated.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	And if the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or water of ashes, then use a cautery of water and honey with a pinch of powdered litarge.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	Or you can cauterize with honey and sweet wine, which has the property of cleaning and washing, and the wine makes the wound burn.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And when you have done this and are certain that the breast is clean, then cauterize with something that makes a crust on it; take a diafinite ointment and mix it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cleanse it with some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken in the section on ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And if the nipple is small and the cannula of the syringe cannot enter, then enlarge it with a knife a little, and insert a tent made of the Egyptian ointment, or the ointment called basilicon, until it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too large, then cut it and leave only the place where the syringe can enter, and if the opening that urinates is above, then cut below it, or higher up, whichever it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowels are perverse, they do not digest food properly;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cut the breast as you wish, then arrange it in such a way that the bowels move to the lowest place they can reach; for when the bowels are perverse, they do not digest food properly. And if you cannot cut the breast as you wish, then arrange it in some other way:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	that the bowels move easily downward, and leave nothing of the bowels behind;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolative medicines to put over the wound, and they are on the linen cloth that covers all the wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cut the opening of the breast more widely than before, then put ointment on the other cloth according to the quantity of the opening, and put it on the wound to loosen the bowels, and do not remove the large cloth but after several days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and the one who is on the opening of the breast, remove often to remove the bowels, and know what comes from the bowels, whether it is poison or a little or enough, or digestion, or indigestion;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been applied in such a way and you see the nature that rises on the wound, then you know that the breast has healed, and the health approaches;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then loosen it in the morning, or at noon, and when you loosen the wound, change the other bandage and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast milk flows strongly after many days, you can be sure that the breast will not dry up.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons run long after a time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are people whose wounds heal slowly, and others that heal quickly;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if milk does not flow from the breast after many days, know that the breast will not produce milk;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breast is delayed in producing milk and is distant, then apply dry medicines that are moist in substance but dry in virtue, such as an ointment of vitriol, for it is the best medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take an ointment of vitriol, and make it with rose oil, and rose water equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	then cook it and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and with the same one makes honey cooked thickened, when ointments of vitriol are not available, or take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them, and sprinkle the powder on the honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then they are bandaged with glue, and the poultice is applied to the chest, and sometimes an aristolongue root, and roots of celestial lilies, which is like flour made from herbs and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and they use simple medicines or compounds:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	They grind them into powder and mix with the honey I mentioned, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the wound is long and not healed by this treatment, then know that the corruption is in depth, and it makes an impression on the bone, or on the hard limbs, or on the tissues;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the wound of the fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the nail abscess
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	A panaris is an abscess that arises under the fingernail of the hand or foot, or perhaps it arises in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it becomes infected and one takes no notice, then the abscess grows, and they grow and burst until they reach the root of the nail, and perhaps they burst all the way;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corrosion to the bone, so that it causes a stinking pain, and the head of the shoulder is swollen with two lumps, and the colour is green-blue.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the previous section, and the treatment is not effective, then you should cut away all the excess tissue that has accumulated beneath the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail presses into the flesh, and starts to grow in, you should cut the nail underneath so that it lifts up from the flesh, and carefully and gently peel off the dead skin, then put on potent and corrosive medications to remove all of it;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and treat the wound, because as long as the corrupt bone remains, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the joint become corrupted, cut it out in an L-shape as described before, then treat the wound until it heals;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wild, and biting, and it feels great pain, then you must heal it first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the fingernail of the spasm with a diagonal cut, being careful that the cutter does not go all the way to the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, place something on it which soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a deaf person's hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two toenails that sometimes grow on the hands of some people by chance are all fleshy, and sometimes they have bones in them, and sometimes they have nails, and some grow from the root of the joint where the nail grows from one of the toes.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those nails that grow from the nailbed do not move, but those that grow from the joint of the toe sometimes do.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The cutting of the fleshy one is thus:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a broad knife.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Those that grow from the root of the joint are painful to treat:
si te tien dou coper.	if you hold it still.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For one who is born with a hernia in the navel at the back, you should first scrape away the flesh roundly up to the bone, then scrape the bone to an appropriate size for that, then heal it until it is well.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together come by birth, or by wound, or by burn, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You must cut the nail, so that the toe can heal according to its natural shape;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two tents or wet cloths in rose oil, so that they do not adhere;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you place between two pieces of thin felt, until the skin is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a person with a sore palm comes to you, then treat that wound as it should be treated.
des vils	of the evil one
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large tubes wrapped in membrane filled with melancholic superfluities that come from various parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more often happens to those who walk on foot and work and carry loads, than to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him an emetic, and then the basil drink.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	There are two methods of using the fire cautery:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is to scorch them, and draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other method is that you open a vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The incision is done in this way:tu traies un petit coup, et puis li traies le sang noir qui y ad
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	you make a small cut, and then draw out the black blood that rises up from it. First warm the leg with very hot water until the veins become subtle, then straighten the leg from above the thigh to the joint below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then cut the vein in one, two or three places, with a large incision, then press and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient can endure;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then the scabs, and he is commanded to dye himself with meats mixed with black soot;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommences the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, which is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The remedies for him are as follows:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	He raises the leg of the patient, if there is much hair on it, then he puts it in a bath and pours hot water over the leg until it turns red and opens the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat it over the fire, and then press down on the vein from above at the knee, or in the part below at the ankle;
