puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the toenail, and scrape the vein from each side, until it appears when you feel it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you will see it red and black, and when it enters into the skin it seems like a white string;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then pour the water beneath it, until it is raised from the skin, and then gently at the edge, then cut in another place above it three times.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then scorch the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it with a tweezers, as you did before, and cut at another edge, as you did before.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then cut another slit, or several if you need to, then lift it and cut at the toe of the foot, then pull and lift up to the second slit.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull it out from slit to slit until it is completely extracted, then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot pull and lift it, then insert a strong doubled thread with a needle, tie it, pull it out, and pour water beneath the vein, turning your hand from side to side until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be sure it does not burst, for if it bursts, one cannot milk or lift it, and the patient suffers harm.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have milked it completely, then place on the site of the wound wool moistened with wine and rose oil;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and enveloped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it twisting, but do not burst it;
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and milk it as we have previously said.Et se li vis est rompiez ou fends en quere de
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	And if the vein is broken or split in the process of removing the iron, the shape of the iron should be curved, and it should not burst the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it should be thick, for if it were slender, it would burst the vein; but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in hot areas where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And sometimes it occurs elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the pustules that emerge under the skin, just as snakes and worms emerge inside the body, between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that a great inflammation comes in the leg, then the color changes, and the wound begins to come out, as well as the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the head is exposed, you must wrap it around with a piece of linen three and a half to four fingers wide, and tie it, leaving the linen hanging down the leg. And every time it dislocates, wrap it again around the linen and the wound.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a part of it and wrap around what remains, but do not cover the root until it is all dislocated.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	Because if you cover it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and pustules at that spot, and great illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	that thing must be treated little by little until the end, and nothing remains in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and sometimes this vein, when it is treated, reaches from the palm of the hand to the elbow, or from the palm to the armpit, and once a man came to me whose vein reached from the palm to the armpit; and when you cut it, insert the needle or probe, and pierce it to the bottom, so that everything comes out.

des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called "cow disease" in our land because it often affects cows, and it is a small worm that grows between the skin and flesh, traveling throughout the body, ascending and descending, and one feels it as it moves from member to member until it breaks through the skin where it goes, and exits.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by an excess of humors, like worms and snakes and roundworms and tapeworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one doubts its maliciousness because when it travels through the body and ascends to the head, if it reaches the eye, it can enter and destroy the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and that happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it traveling through the body, one cannot stop it until it leaves:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so you must tie the area above and below with a strong string tightly, then cut it out and if the worm is deep in the flesh, and you cannot extract it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it runs in the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye, grab the eyelash firmly underneath and pull it out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and one should use the patient's body purification with medicinal solutions to draw out the bad humors, and wash with meats that cause swelling.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called 'visceritis' in our land, and it is a pain that comes in one member, and then moves from member to member;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of her elbow;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and soon after, I saw it rising up her shoulder like a worm, quickly and brightly like silver when it moves from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain leaves that area and settles in the shoulder, and then a little later it runs through the whole body until it reaches the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then it started twisting around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how she moved from limb to limb like that, because I had never seen this illness behave in that way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I have seen many whose pain moved from one place to another, but I did not see it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that it was because a woman's body is dry and their veins are exposed, and because this windiness is forced out;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they did not experience it according to this reason in those who were sick, who had moist bodies and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see this disease being treated, and the patient feels the pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then apply pressure above and below, and then press gently until that forced windiness leaves the area;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the area;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it yourself, then the doctor who treats wind-related ailments, as with foul-smelling pills, and serapium pills, and similar remedies.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, depending on their appearance and the place in the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of their appearance is that some have large points, some small, some have heads, and some are bald;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	Some have two angles, some have tongues, and some have pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	And those that break in a limb break in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Or in a principal member it breaks, like the brain, heart, liver, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members. Or it breaks in a subsidiary member, like the limbs:
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it therefore breaks in any of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you about appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	Then you should beware of extracting this arrow, for death comes after in many cases;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not entirely out, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of a trepanation wound is when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and the syphilis breaks through the skull, and there is scotomata and pain and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of blood:
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps it comes out through the nose or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps they lose their speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the wound comes white moisture resembling pus, and also like blood-clots;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then stop the treatment and pull out the arrow if it is still inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of a wound to the heart are that it is near the left breast, and it feels as if it were pierced into a hard object, not bleeding;Et quant li saiettes chiet entre le col et li poitrins, et s’il est enflammiez et gonfliez, si est grant dolor.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the patient becomes mute like the fowl, and turns pale, and there is dark blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then you will know without doubt that death has occurred.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow wound that never leaves the body is foam without pain, emerging from the wound, and a swollen throat, and the patient's colour changing, and gasping for breath and seeking the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow pierces the scrotum, it is near the testicles;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and there is great pain and sighing;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the limbs move from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow pierces the heart or stomach, by chance something indigestible may come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces the belly and nothing comes out through the intestines but feces, there is no hope for a cure nor for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow pierces the bladder, and the urine flows out in a jet and there is bleeding, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	then you will know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, armpit, spine of the back, buttock, thigh, and leg, and similar members, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and is not poisonous, as I will tell you so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow hit him in the jaw, in the root of the teeth:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I probed it, and drew it out from under the ear, and he was healed without any numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And take an arrow and shoot it into the fat of the eye below the eyelid, and the arrow was wrapped around, and one could only touch its point towards the shaft, and the arrow was as big as a Turkish bow, all of iron, without ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	the games were healthy, and no bad accidents happened.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And take an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I shaved the beards, and subtly shot it so that I hit him, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And take an arrow from a man who has it in his head or belly, and think that he will die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after thirty days, his condition did not improve;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and pushed it out, and he had no bad accident.Et ot un oileier qu’ot une saiette en la cuisse, si com il li traioit la saiette;
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a person whom an arrow has hit in the back, and the wound is closed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remains inside him, and his natural functions are undisturbed and he experiences no discomfort in any of his natural processes.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And you see another man whom an arrow has hit in the face, and the wound is closed over;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and he remains thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And treat an arrow that has hit the king's son in the head, and is lodged in his brain, and he is slightly nghiêng to the right;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow is fully embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat him after three days had passed.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I examined him thoroughly, and I did not feel anything;Et si vis I home cui il chut un saiette en la paume de sa main dreite, et ne demora li
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the tip of the arrowhead. I placed a soothing and digestive poultice on the area, so that the ears would not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the head of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the poultice for several days, and the wound healed quickly, and the patient felt the arrow inside his nose for a long time;
et il le me dist.	and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it healed, and I tested it, and felt the tip of the arrow which was protruding out;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then, I adjusted the opening of the wound using that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow became visible to me;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and let him transgress the terms for 4 months, and then tear open the wound that I clamped with tweezers, and pull from one side and the other, and it cannot come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	therefore I did not cease to use instruments and invent ways, until one day I took the tweezers well-made, according to what his form will be in the end of this chapter, as I drew it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And let them judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it therefore, and the wound was closed, and the patient was completely healed.And in a similar case, I found an arrow in the shoulder of a man who had been struck by an arrow through the neck, which had entered below the ear, and gone out at the shoulder
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your care upon what I do not say, for the book cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the wise masters consider well very little, and what is present and lacking to them, they devise new work, and new instruments, in the descent of strange things which come about in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows grow in the limbs where they are stuck in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the place where they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which goes out through the place where it entered is an arrow entering into the flesh, and sometimes goes out immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not go out immediately, leave it until the flesh around it becomes rotted away, and loosen the exit;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot go out, then leave it for several days, and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will come out, and if not, then pierce around it with a very thin instrument until the flesh around it is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the skull, and goes right through to one of the membranes of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	don't pull it out, but let it be until it is even with the skin for a few days, for if the arrow pierces to the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not reach the brain, and the patient remains for several days without any bad signs, then try to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is pierced deeply and cannot be pulled out, then apply cauterization around it as I have told you:
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then clean the wound until it is healed.Et s’il est encores maladiz, si covient qu’il soit baigne en l’
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in the body so that it cannot be seen, then it must be sought throughout the body;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, pull it out with an appropriate instrument;si ne le puet demorer en li cors, si la laisse tant qu’elle soit igals, et met
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then open it as much as the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs that hold it in place, then cut away the flesh where it is stuck on both sides as much as you can, and then bend or twist the barbs of the arrow until you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the arrow, so that you can pull it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot extract it in one go, then leave it until the surrounding area becomes swollen; then pull it out, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding is too profuse, then follow what we have said about stopping the bleed in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of cutting into a nerve or vein, and use any means you can to pull out the arrow safely, quickly or slowly, gently or forcefully;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient in the position he was in when the arrow struck him, for that is the greatest aid you can provide; and if you cannot, then place him according to the signs that the stars show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	Arrows that come from another direction, or where some of it protrudes, or the skin is swollen in that spot, either visibly or felt by touch:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	cut above it, as high as the tweezers can reach, and then extract it:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it is a through-and-through wound.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, rotate your hand rapidly, so that it goes into the bone and widens the opening, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be extracted, then leave it for now and try again later to extract it;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is an arrowhead in it, push it all the way through;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the shaft is short, and you intend to administer a tourniquet, then place the arrowhead into the hole of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then pushed out, and if the arrow is lodged in the head, he pushes the instrument in point first to ease extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow has touched, you must cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then cure the wound as it should be done.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits the leg or foot or belly or bladder or side, and it is close to the surface, and you can cover it with your hand, then cup it;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cover the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then cut the wound if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat the wound until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to treat arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	There are many ways to do this:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the feathered end is also like the feathers on an arrow, to catch and stick to the tip of the arrow, as shown in the illustration.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for pushing and probing if it's there:
des voinnes dou cors communes	veins of the common body:
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are 31 types of veins from which one can bleed, and in the head there are 16 of them, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two veins located behind the ears, called the "two hares";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are in the two temples visible;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the veins that are in the lids of the eyes, which are called "aspirers";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two windpipes which are in the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above the lips at the mouth, and they are the veins that are called "augerich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly used for bleeding are five in each arm:La premiere qui est apeleee  «Veine de la Main» qui se prend ad le coté del coeur
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	The first which is called the "Vein of the Hand" which is taken from the side of the heart, one is the cephalic, and it is from the left side, and people call it the "vein of the head";La seconde qui est appellee  «Veine de l’avant-bras»
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the means is called "fasting", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and the common people call it "vein of the heart";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic is on the right side, and the common people call it  "vein of the belly", and it is above the sacrum, and it is the one that opens clearly above the scrotum.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And  the salvator is the vein between the little finger and ring finger, and has two branches:
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is under the crook of the scrotum on the left side, and the second is at the ankle on the right side;and the third is:
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein that is called "thigh", which is at the ankle of the other side;and all these three veins come together and form a single vein, which goes up along the inside of the leg:
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below them.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears helps with old cataracts and with migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the bleeding is as I told you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then press on the neck of the patient with your thumb, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places under the head;
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	hold them there and where you feel the pulse below your finger, press inwards;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lance and pierce below the vein right to the bone, then lift your hand up along the vein, and press and pierce through the skin and the vein for two fingers length, and let the blood out until you see enough;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strain and bind it, until it is healed
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the temples is useful for old migraines, and sore eyes, and constant tearing, and for the eyes of those with ague;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the bleeder are as I have said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and the patient should stretch his neck so that the two veins can be seen clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	feel for the pulse in your groin, and then sign with a cross;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lightly cut the vein at the top of your index finger, and insert the lance underneath, and open the vein at the top, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then loosen the bandage, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then form a blister, and leave it until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken of them and their treatment and extraction in the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding from the vein on the forehead is just as good for ancient diseases of the face, and for migraine, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is such that the patient turns his neck until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument which is called "digging", of which here is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and press with your hand, or something else, and let the blood issue according to the amount you want;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then tie off the vein, and let it heal and sometimes use a wide flame.Et s’il est necessaire qu’on le remette a leu, tu resaisies la voinne;
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too fierce;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the blood flows sideways, for the bone is close by, and the flame may break it when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bloodletting of the two veins that are in the two temples helps with headaches, and eye problems, and facial diseases;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the nature of their bloodletting is such that the patient turns his neck by twisting it with a bandage, as described earlier;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then bloodlet, and let the cut be deep, but the flame not too wide, for there is no bone there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame is thin, it may break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then let the blood flow, as much as you need, and then bind it up tightly with a thread.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The bleeding of the vein in the nose is good for nosebleeds and sudden fainting spells, and for facial illnesses such as the migration of redness and bumps that appear on the face, especially when they are chronic.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	And the quality of this bleeding is that you should squeeze your patient's neck, then pinch his nose with your left hand, and take a long, thin flame and insert it into the lip space between the two nostrils because the vein does not open well, and the blood will now begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go in too deeply, just let the blood flow according to your need, then ligature it for one night, because it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is how you make the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	Bleeding the two veins helps with throat constrictions, and with many illnesses, and with swelling, and with scurvy, and with herpes and ulcers.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of the healing are such that the patient stretches his neck below one and then the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and the master stands above the patient's head, and the patient lies on a bed, then the long vein is cut widely, then the blood is bled moderately, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then do the same to the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and gently squeeze the veins, so that the patient is not strangled;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave it until the morning, so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	of bleeding from the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bleeding from the veins of the lips above helps with cold in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and splitting of the lips, and toothache and pain in the jaw.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the healing are such that the patient sits in front of you, and stretches his neck as I have said;Et tu sieces sus li chief, et li malaides sus I siege ou la lit, puis saine la voinne dou lonc un poc largement, et trai dou sang tempreement ou tant com mestier est.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then do the same to the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and gently squeeze the veins, so that the patient is not strangled;And let it be until the morning, so that the wound heals.And the qualities of the healing are such that the patient sits in front of you, and stretches his neck as I have said;You stand above the head, and the patient sits or lies on the bed, then cut the long vein widely, and bleed the blood moderately, or as much as is necessary.Then turn around, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left,
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Take therefore one of each, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, take the largest of each, and do likewise to the two veins above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	And the qualities of bleeding under the tongue: have the patient stick out his tongue and grip it from below with your left hand; then take a sharp knife and cut both sides of the frenulum, and cut straight through until you reach the muscle, and then pull the tongue down so that it hangs down. Then hold the tongue steady with your left hand and grasp the frenulum with your right hand, pulling it up towards the nose as far as you can, while cutting with a knife under the root of the tongue; when you have finished cutting, let go with your left hand and with your right pull it up towards the nose until it comes away. Then take a piece of wool and put it over the wound to stop the bleeding, and let him spit out the blood that has collected in his mouth.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bleeding of the veins below the tongue aids after the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it is for the narrowing of the throat, and for diseases of the gullet, and for diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the qualities of the bleeder are such that he should cut between his fingers in front of the sun, and raise his tongue, and look under each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Bleed therefore one and then the other, and do not go too deep, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the neck, from which one bleeds commonly, are bled in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	where it pricks at their base, hold them steady so they do not move until they grow.
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and narrow according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame martin is very renowned, and it is broad as you can see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open flat veins filled with thick, visible blood, and that contain thick, troubled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the flame olive:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed and is for bleeding subtle veins, where there is subtle yellow blood.The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and the surgeon must bleed it, and he must be careful of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if it pierces the artery, and blood flows out, then it must be staunched, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the flame should not be pierced, but cut like an onion.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basil doesn't open clearly, then you must strain it and change to another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you want a vein from him, or you heal in his place the vein in the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the cup to the flame extinguishes, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to find the place of bleeding, then you must stretch out the arm, and touch the place until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with ink, and then tie up the arm, and cup the vein with the flame extinguished;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and be careful not to pierce an artery when you see the place puffed up, for it is an artery:
eschui la donques.	avoid it therefore.Et si li poulz ne poigne en la sain
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if the pulse does not beat in the bleeding, and you see it rise up as high as urine from a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	So you quickly, and put your finger over the wound for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	bind the arm and leave it like that, and don't move it, so that the patient does not feel any pain;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be careful not to move it until the bleeding stops.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the wound won't stop bleeding and you don't have any medicine, cut open the artery where it is bleeding from the most, because that's where the blood is coming out from.
et estainche li sans.	Then stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a piece of bark from an oak tree, split it in half, and use one half to bind the wound tightly until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	If the bleeding stops, that's good;si li sans ne s’estainchie pas, adonques lie li bras, et
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If it doesn't stop, then bind the arm tightly, and if that doesn't work either, then use one of the powders that stops bleeding, as we said before.Et s’il adonques li sans ne vait point, et ne lie
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the bandages are not wrapped in various positions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The bleeding of the vein in the middle helps that it draws blood from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and the surgeon must be careful not to pierce too deeply and to find the nerve below, and if he pierces it too much the nerve will inflame and the wound will become infected and may not heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve often opens up, and if it does not open in some people due to its subtlety, you must treat it with the anaesthetic tool;et li nerf de la mainne apert a la coze de la piere, et si covient qu’on le saine del sainement de l’estrument, et s’il ne poait gueres estre sans estainche, il convient qu’il fie
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and avoid the nerve at your own risk.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, they cut it from the long one.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The surgery on the cephalic vein helps, drawing blood from the head, and helping the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is best to lance with an olive-wood or myrtle-wood point, for it is the safest of all veins, for there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, one must seek the lightest vein, and not hurt anything if one misses the first time, and try again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance, some people's veins swell up when they miss the first time, but it doesn't hurt them.Si est raide ou dur, si covient sainier as deux flasques, car li dur corps demere plus qu’on ne fait la voinne
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bloodletting depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you should know about lancing is that it is not done to cure illness, but rather to prevent diseases from coming;et por ce covient sainier la venie qui est plus pres li malaides, car par celle venie que le sang s’en va, il revient a la santeit.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins that are in the neck:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, cephalic, fast, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed in the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion are apparent;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should bleed on the first day or third day, after two hours or three of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding administered for illnesses has no set time, but whenever the need arises, day or night, at all times and in all seasons;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one should not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor women carrying a child before the fourth month up to the seventh month.Quant la maladie est en la teste et en la fumee de la teste;
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the very old be bled who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when one wishes to be bled in any manner, one should first cleanse the bowels with a mild clyster if they are holding back much feces so that the veins do not draw harmful excesses from the intestines into the principal limbs;Car la fiens retentée, par son poids et sa pesance, attire li sang de les membres en bas vers la fumee de la teste:
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	He who is too fat from eating meat, or who is drunk, as much as he may be, nor a person with dropsy will not heal.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one is made better after colic, vomiting, diarrhea, and frequent intercourse with a woman, and from exertion, staying up late, and fasting, and that which comes from the use of weapons or from the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly alter the humors, if they are thick, through food and drink and medicine, if you have the power to do so;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter the bath, if nothing else weakens him, to alter the blood, and heal from the vein around the third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and beware of exertion, piercing, and luxury, and similar things that day;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be calm and cheerful, and let the healer stand higher than the one being healed, and rub the arm 2 or 3 times, then tighten the bandage above the wound, for if it is too loose or too tight, it will not work;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area with your hands, until the veins swell, and you can feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then moisten the cautery with a little old oil, then put your finger from your left hand onto that vein underneath where you want to cauterize, so that the vein does not burst and split when you touch it.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	Because there are veins that flow like cords when cauterized, and some are filled with wind, so that when you touch them with the cautery, the cautery draws back and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with some.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if he opens the vein, but the wound is too narrow for that, then the cauterizer must be skilled in such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good;and if not, then you must touch it with a hot stone, as will now be said.Et si il ne fu
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then begin again a little lower than the place where there is swelling.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the arm is swollen and the patient is in doubt, then leave it for a day or two, and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	by chance there will be pus-filled abscesses.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter the bath, then begin the bleeding again if she wishes;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the vein is small, open it carefully and gently in that same vein directly;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work on it gently, until the arm swells.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this often happens when the vein is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the vein swollen, do not begin bleeding again, but put a little linseed oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the oil is medicine.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil mixture to each wound that you treat veins with, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this same mixture makes a poultice and bandage for them when one puts it on the spot;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if subtly the blood escapes and is split when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes great abscesses, which often happen, especially when it is not treated before the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put damp sponges in warm water on the spot and hold them for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you must do this after the flow of blood from the vein, and if it remains on the spot for some days, there will be no harm;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see anything of aloe or myrrh mixed with juice of hellebore, or similar, put it on the spot.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times abscesses and appearances occur at the opening of the basilic vein:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	put your hand over it, and if you find the place soft to the touch, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Therefore, avoid putting anything on it of what we have described, for perhaps it is close to an artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to its quantity and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it turns red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for one who is full and bloated, and needs bloodletting, they should make a larger wound, and the flames should be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for the weak, do the opposite, and one must bleed them little by little often, and they should be bled by cutting diagonally, not by pricking;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this bleeding method is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and it is better than bleeding the long or the large vein.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for those whose body needs bleeding, one should give them moist bread in pomegranate juice;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If they are hot-tempered, let them eat moist bread with pomegranate juice three or four times before bleeding. And if of a cold temperament, let them eat moist bread with syrupy muzel, or with aromatic honey syrup and spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicory, and perfumed syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he faints after losing a lot of blood, then he should drink warm broth and subtle scented syrup, and use the other remedies we mentioned in the chapter on syncope for opening a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to empty his arm and bleed again, then when he is weakened by a large bleeding, he should bleed a little at a time according to the amount of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to open their arm after the first bleeding, and they have strong pulses, then heal for .vii. hours after the first bleeding, or after the new hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to bleed from another part, then they should bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For they have a lot of blood inside their body which is hot and causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if one must draw a great quantity, and widen the hole so that it is cut by the lance;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you must examine all the signs of healing, and place your hand over the pulse when it is healing, so that death does not come to the lance-wound, and this happens many times when the surgeon is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it must not be, when you see the arm being released and blood emerging a second time, and the hole is closed, that you press directly on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is crooked, that it extends the arm suddenly, for that would be bad;puis que li fies la cure a la fin, et demourra en leu de pameson, si li sainieres ne fu pas negl
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	then you must perform the treatment at the end, and let it remain in place until it heals a second time; but if the surgeon was negligent,
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you may touch it with the tip of the flame, until the frozen blood at the wound's entrance melts, and place a little salt in water, and press gently on it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and don't constrict it until the abscess is drained.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it's necessary to let blood a second time, then bleed in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	Veins in the arm are bled in the area of the vein near the shoulder because it is closer to the heart.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing is for the patient to put his hand in hot water until the wart turns red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then let it be cut slightly, so that the vein appears well, then heal it immediately from the inside, not from the wide nor the long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the slit be wide, and let it be healed near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, then put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer, then do not put the hand back in hot water, for it is warmer in summer than in winter;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the healing of this vein is safer than any other vein, that there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of the salvation of the right hand is for all diseases of the liver, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	hold the hand, and pour hot water on it until the vein is swollen, if one can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it is cut across, and you bandage it firmly from all sides, then it will not be painful.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	do not go too deep, because the nerves are completely stripped of flesh underneath; and then put the hand back in hot water if the blood has congealed in the wound, so that it can flow out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as necessary, put oil and silk on the vein to heal quickly, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is good for the disease of the mumps, and do everything just as I have told you about the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sauce of the sophia is good for all diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the kidneys, and retention of fluids, and diseases of the intestines, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And in terms of how to treat it, the patient should put his foot in hot water and rub the vein until it breaks, and tie something around the ankle joint;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and if the vein is at the ankle, there will be many veins going up the foot.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	So treat it in the widest vein, or at the ankle, whichever is easiest to access.Et si li voinne ne puet pere en aigue chaude, et se li sans est dedenz la plaie congele
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you heal it on the foot, then beware of the nerves that are underneath, and heal it across as well as upwards by cutting.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flames be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the pus cannot come out, then put the foot into water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the healing fails the first time, then try again a second time on top of it, for the wound is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt about nerve, as we have said, and thus do with the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The site of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its remedy is for pain in the hip, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the nature of its healing is that the patient goes into the bath, and twists above the ankle three times, for otherwise the vein does not open;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then heal it in all the ways that you can, and by cutting across;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better to cut than to burn, for the wound is safe, and it is very painful for many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not believe this, then test any vein that opens on the front or back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful with the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	And let blood flow until you see it, then untie the ligature and place cotton over it and compress it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of cupping glasses
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cupping glasses are made from horns, or brass, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and cupping is performed according to two methods:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cupping without cutting is performed in two ways:ou par cautere, ou par foyre;
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either with fire, or without fire; it can be done with all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and cupping that is performed by cutting and drawing blood is done in 14 places on the body, of which one is entirely on the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are within the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and the others are on both sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the cupping glass under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the cupping glasses on the shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping glass above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the cupping glasses within both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the cupping glasses on both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cupping glasses on the ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and bloodletting does not treat any vein, except for small veins that are scattered throughout the body, and because of this it does not weaken one in the slightest, as is done with phlebotomy;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it must not be administered, nor at any heat or fever, in any disease that comes from fullness, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, due to necessity or habit, bloodletting must be done, then we do it every hour at the beginning and end of the month, and throughout all times of the year.Et si li corps n’est vuidiez par ventose, on ne le doit mie ventoser en tel tens, si com qu’il soit vuidiez;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are those who, when they need to fart, feel great pressure.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and some experience congestion and redness in their face, head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and some bleed from their mouth, have a swollen tongue, and taste blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and some dream, and see through the night terrible things and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially if it is during the month, we command them to fast after 3 hours of the day.
