Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bleeding from the nose helps the headache ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not good for this to happen after the evacuation of the whole body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this venting is in the place of bleeding from the head, and it is not good for those who are of a cold complexion to do it, or who have a catarrh, because it does them great harm;et si convient qu’il soit aprés le sainie de la Cephalique;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason the elderly should not use it, nor those with serious illnesses.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal often become blind, and because of this, one must place the cupping glass a little lower down due to the fear of blindness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Ventilation is in the neck, for the relief of headache and toothache, and for constriction of the chest, and for splitting of the channel of the stomach, and for all kinds of swelling and bloating.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it should not be applied too strongly, as if it holds too tightly, it causes injury to the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	Ventilation at the second rib of the neck helps with headaches, and eye pain and inflammation, and constriction, and dental pain, and is in the place for relieving toothache.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and you must instruct the operator to express his hand while putting it on, so that he does not squeeze the artery and cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	Windings underneath the chin help with mouth diseases, and gum decay, and similar illnesses that occur in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and cause suppuration between the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilation of the armpits is good for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	Windings on the sides help as much as three veins in the arm, because they attract blood from those large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the surgeon not to go too deep, because the area is bare of flesh and contains nerves and arteries underneath;
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping glass placed on the buttocks helps with hemorrhoids and diseases underneath, and it should be large, made of copper, and good at drawing;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And if it were subtle, it would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	Cupping glasses on the legs heal very well, because they attract blood from the whole body, and help with long-standing pains in the kidneys, and the womb, and the bladder, and bring back period flow;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are located in the two sockets, and in the two ankles, and nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and cause paralysis in many ways.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply the cupping glass is that you first place it empty, and suck gently, and place it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing so until you see the area red and swollen, and the color of blood appears.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then heat it, and put on the cupping glasses again, taking care to observe the condition of the body, as there are those with very thin skin and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	It is necessary to pierce only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a little deep;and if the blood does not come well, heat again.
et suce legierement.	and suck gently.If the blood does not come well, heat again.Et s
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to pierce twice:first you make a wound wide and a little deep, and when the blood comes, you pier
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to open the path of thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, then it is necessary to pierce a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw little by little, we only do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want a lot of blood, we start over again often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, we pierce deeply and the veins are pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those who have thick and tough skin, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the places where the leeches will be placed with an astringent oil and a dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in the head, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or squash seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in the liver, use watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, take oil of amaranth, or of balsamite, or aniseed oil, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if those to whom one heals have soft flesh and wide pores, no oil should be put on them, but they should be washed after cupping with rosewater, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture, if they rise from garlic, or myrrh water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large swollen areas rise from old wine, or from pure water, or from a decotion of anise or camomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it is not appropriate to bleed by cupping before the bath or in the bath itself, but one or two hours after the bath.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and he should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary for him to be careful, both when he is being cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware if the person being bled is choleric, and if the blood is too thin and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	then he should eat cool things like pomegranates, endives, lettuce with garlic, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and drink mead, and wine mixed with vinegar, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those of a cold complexion should eat honey syrup, and moderate old wine, and drink mead, and drink mead, and eat small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day he is bled, he must drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men garlic or musk before or after bleeding to strengthen the main organs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and dilute the wine, but those who are hot-tempered should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The ventouses that are used without burning are those that are placed over the liver, and the mumps, and the scurvy, and over the belly, the armpits, the thighs, and the groin, because these members cannot bear to be burned, and it is only done to draw blood from one member into another, as we put them on breasts when babies suckle.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity that is in a member, just like we put ventouses over the belly and armpit to reduce the swelling of the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and removes the pain when there is a stone or tumor, and by its attractive power it removes the tumor or pushes the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and similarly, when placed on the liver and on the abdomen when there is retained wind, and these cupping glasses are administered empty in order to suck only slightly.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water in which suitable herbs have been boiled; in such cases the water is used only once.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cup to be administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	It is two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and on the side near the middle it has a small hole, just big enough to push through a needle; it should be made of brass, smooth in front so as not to hurt the patient when placed on the body.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	In the middle it has a cross-bar of brass or iron, to hold a candle, and they come in various sizes according to the sickness and age of those who use them. They can be large or small.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	Because children's bellows are different from adults', and thin people's from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should thus place this bellows on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the candle of wax or the linen, and place it inside the bellows through the tube which is inside the bellows, so that the flame is at the bottom of the bellows and does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and your fingers should be on the hole that we have mentioned, so that when one wishes, the vapor goes out, and then remove the bellows;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and use the linen just as before, and repeat it often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	The bellows which is used for pleurisy and all wounds has no tube or hole, but is placed on the limb only when it is full of water.
et c’est li forme:	and this is how you do it:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Leeches are not applied except in parts where cups cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on bare flesh, such as ears or nose, and other similar areas;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of their use is such that when you apply leeches that are in clean, still water without any odor, they will attach themselves;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in fresh water for as long as they are accustomed to it and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	then cleanse the vein and apply cups, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place the leeches on top;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and begin to bite, if it is a place where cups can be applied, then do so, for it is much better.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then raise the area with ash, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it out.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the bites are too close to the body of the snake, then soak a linen cloth in cold water and place it over the bite until the swelling goes down.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if there are many bites, then apply ground vitriol, or gall, and similar things, until the swelling goes down.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you can place half-peeled beans on the bite, and leave them until they turn green, this will stop the swelling immediately.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more of it, catch other snakes.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the snakes don't want to be caught, then rub the wound with fresh blood, or stab it with a needle until the venom comes out, and then place them over the bite. As soon as they smell the blood, they will start to lick it;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see them defecating, powder some aloe and salt, or ashes, over a little, and they will stop immediately.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and is for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the fools mock this chapter, which they have never seen in any ancient book or letter.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason the science is strange in our land, for I never found anyone good at it;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and know nothing about it, except through the science of ancient books, and I have studied it so much that I have gained knowledge through it, and through experimentation, and through my own experience;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained in it, and have abbreviated it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say in the prologue to this book that the subjects of the discussion and the chapters in which the sage places his understanding, and dwells upon the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or bruising affects someone, you should hurry to treat the patient from one side and the other, if nothing holds them back, as with weakness of body, or pregnancy, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the weather is very hot, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and eat cool foods, that is to say, cold games, and pheasant and rabbit meat, and do not drink any wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill yourself too much with food that fills the veins with blood, until you have suspected a hot abscess or spreading of matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the illness returns to its first state of governance which it has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, one must feed the patient foods that promote swelling and viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testes, pigs' feet, pig's belly, offal, fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Because with more swelling the break will be closed more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot heal well or unite according to their nature due to the dryness of the members, nor those that are also too tender, like the bones of young children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but it does not matter, reset over the broken bone the large tendons that stretch and join the limb together, as much as it enforced like it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not give up on his work, and for this reason one should nourish with large amounts of food, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures come in many forms and manners.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg; and I will tell you in this chapter about all types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture which goes to the bone, and another in puncturing, like the tip of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break all over a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in every way it has its own method and tool for restoration according to the memory that comes to mind;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the fracture of the bone is known by its twisting, and it appears well on the outside, and sounds hollow when pressed with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting nor any sound when touched, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can still have twisting, or splitting, or a small fracture.Et si li chiés est desaloiez, ou la cuisse, et ne puet demorer en son leu por cause
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You must not move it by hand, but apply the medicines that follow, and then hold it firmly but gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that goes into the bone, and the two parts are separated, they must now be set evenly, so that abscesses do not form.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if a hot abscess forms, he should leave it for one day, until the abscess is soothed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	Then he sets it even as quickly and gently as possible, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restoration of that one where there is a break.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then he binds it, as appropriate, afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there is a break in the bone, if it is in two parts, whether it is the hand or foot, or the arm, or a small limb, with two strings, or one string and the hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And he sets the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are set right, then with all his skill, he brings the additions back into their places as he can, and guards against causing the patient injury or pain through his work.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust both heads of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it by hand if it doesn't seem right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if you dress it nicely and don't pull or press too hard as those who bring about hot abscesses and constriction in the limb through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the joint is healed, instruct the patient to not move it, not while waking, sleeping, turning, or in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and be careful that the limb is secure so that he feels no pain.Si li membres sent douleur de lor chiés des os ou de lor costes et les poingनत, si leve tant com il
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, then it is not healed, and you should put it in such a position that he feels no pain;Si li membres est trop mal figurez ou trop desaloiez, si doit on le rimetre en tel ovraige qu’il soit bellement dreit et si covient le res
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and make sure it is put back straight so that no crookedness comes to it when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken member are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You should know that broken members are diverse in smallness and size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small members like arms and fingers and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	one must wrap them in soft and thin linen;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, like thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	one must wrap them in a wide and firm bandage, for the wide bandages embrace the whole large member and constrict it evenly all around so that there is no swelling;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie light sponges around it, three or four times according to the member, and press your hand on all the bandage, then go above the dislocation and press less, so that the dislocation moves a little away from the dislocation;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the ligament little by little, until you grip a large part of the healthy area, then take another ligament, and turn back around on the broken area;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go to the part under the break, and grip it gently, not too hard or too softly, as we have said in the first hour above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the ligaments pieces of linen or rags, until they are all even, then tie it all above with the bandage, and then put your splints on well, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put something hot that soothes the abscess on top, and let it be like that for several days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then grip the splints and have them be of half a palm width made from a branch of a willow tree, or from a palm frond, and have them be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but one must ensure that the star that is placed on the fracture is a little larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and as long as it is convenient for the limb, according to its smallness or بزرگی؛
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then press on the stars as you did at the first time, then tie a thread over them, just like you did at the first time on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter it is, the better; if it's too tight, then loosen it a little;si li membres ne se mue
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the member must not move, and one should use a thin thread that is not too thick nor too thin, and it should be made of soft flax;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	because if the threads are thick, as I have seen fools make their laces with twisted cords, and this is a great error, for the lace cannot be even if it is too thin, and there should not be less than two fingers of space between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is weak after the stretching in their healthy arms, then place beneath them a pad of linen or other soft cloth so that they do not hurt themselves.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment for it later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that one should not dislocate all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when a member is swollen, you should not put a splint on it for more than five or seven days, or longer depending on the security of the hot abscess.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And here is the manner of ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And you should take flour that is kept on the walls of the mill, and cook it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring fractures in various conditions, especially in women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of plaster restoring fractures, dislocations and twists:Prend de l’huile d’olives clere et fine, et en faiz une pate avec farine dou molin, et que la
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take clear and fine olive oil, and make a paste with flour from the mill, and take three barleycorns and ladani and inula and asafetida and gum arabic and mastic, each 10;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloe, each 5 drams;
alechil VIIII З.;	aloe wood VIIII drams;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	grind them into powder and mix with egg yolk;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and helps to set broken bones and heals many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another way of making a plaster that helps with twisting injuries:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take mugwort and bee's wax, each 1/5 ounce;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloe, each 3 drachms;
acaice VI З.;	acacia gum 2 drachms;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	armenian bole 1/5 ounce, and grind well, and simmer with water or egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another recipe for an ointment for joints and bones displaced from their sockets, which relieves pain, shrinks the swelling, and promotes healing of broken bones:Pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take new lamb's wool, and boil it in vinegar and oil, and apply it to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing hot abscesses and relieving pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another recipe for an ointment which restores broken bones:Pren vismalve et mugat, ana X З.;
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take bee's wax and mugwort, each 1/5 ounce; take dried fig leaves and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together to make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make an ointment for the healing of broken bones and to reduce inflammation from an abscess: take equal parts honey, vinegar, and lard; boil them together and apply it to the affected area.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take equal parts of the root of viscum album, chamomile flowers, violet flowers, and wheat flour.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Grind the ingredients together and mix with wine. If the member is hot, mix with coriander water or water and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of making a plaster stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take equal parts of the roots of viscum album, flax seeds, borage, melilot, and sanicle, as well as violet and chamomile flowers.Grind them together and mix with wine. If the member is hot, mix with coriander water or water and apply it.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Grind them together and mix with salt water, fresh water, or wine, depending on the temperature of the member and its condition. If the member is hot, mix with coriander water or water and apply it.Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypocras writes in his book that one should not put anything on a broken member to restore it other than a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be between soft and too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen says one should put on the broken member, to restore, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take the beards and hair of humans, or bird feathers, and viscacha fur, all equally, and grind them up to make a poultice which you apply to it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	Then loosen it a little later, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain or move the bone out of place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if you don't loosen it by hand after a few days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the area, or itching, with rest or swelling, hurry and loosen it, and remove the poultice immediately;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a sponge from the sea, moistened in water, and apply it to the area until the itching stops and the pain is soothed;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply lamb's wool dipped in water or rose oil, and lay it on a mat, until you are sure there is no hot abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and relieve the inflammation of the member, and remove the pain, then restart the subtle ligature, and a little ointment, and do not constrict as strongly as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen, and you need ointment and binding, then restart it in the same way as before.Et se li maux sont jai osté dou tout, et li membra sont jai sane, si ne fitz mie ren de la lieure ne de l’emplaustre; mes s’il est encores dolor, et enfleure, et roujor, si fitz ren come tu a fait avant.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing comes of what we have said to the member, do not disentangle it until after 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And sometimes leave it for 20 days, according to what one sees, until the fracture is healed and the flesh approaches;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then restrain it more than before, and increase its meat, as I said before.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	And if you see the place drier than necessary, know that healing cannot come;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Therefore rise it with warm water, every time you disentangle it, and every third day, and loosen the ligature a little;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	through this work therefore shorten the limbs, and gently mend that which fools destroy, who restore the limb crookedly:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it is cruel, and those who work it are fearful, and I see nothing else but wearying oneself and doing it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various methods of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many kinds of fractures, and various shapes, and the causes are distinct;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures that are made by the impact of a sword, and the collar bone is broken all the way to the hyoid bone which is below the collar bone, as a neck or a pole does;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and because of this that kind of fracture is called "neck-fracture".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, and this kind of fracture is called  "complete";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and the wound of these two fractures are large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a deep impact, or a split or blow from a stone, or falling on stone, or other similar occurrences.The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a penetrating fracture which approaches the membrane that is below the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is lodged in the bone as subtly as a hair, and the split is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is made by stone or by falling, or in a similar way, and it drives the piece of bone down, and the place is split like the way that blacksmiths split kettles when they forge them;
si entre li piere dedens.	if the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to those who have moist bones at the top, like the head of a child;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens with all these types of fractures that small pieces are dislocated like tiles;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the distraction upon them and the examination at night, and by the foul smell that is upon it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairline fracture is known by this: when one has exposed the bone and rubs it, the black crack appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, take care of the accidents of illness, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of consciousness, and extension, and palpitations, and fever, and eyes popping out and turning red, and others similar in various dispositions, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a miraculous event, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the newborn comes to you first, and it is in winter, then you should remove the foreskin before the fourteenth day that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the spring, then you should hurry to remove the foreskin before the seventh day so that the tissue underneath the foreskin does not decay and cause the problems we have described.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches just up to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part thus:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and you must grab the head of the patient, and expose the bone in all ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more gently than you can, and if bleeding occurs when exposing the bone, or a pus-filled abscess, treat it with what is appropriate, and you must fill the area with soft rags soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the pus-filled abscess is soothed, and be sure that there is no more bleeding;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin around the bone to remove it, and this can be done in two ways:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one way is to cut closely in front, and that is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put on another bandage larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second way is to have many different cuts, some narrow and some wide, and they should be pointed, and made of steel;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work gently so you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is thick and hard, you should pierce around it, so that you administer trepanning with borers, not so deep that it penetrates through to the brain case, and there should be a rim or ring on top of the tip, preventing the tip from penetrating beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you should have several of these, so that each one comes into its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you have borers for all parts of the skull;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and these are the forms of the three types of borers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing around a broken bone is that you place the borer on the bone and turn it with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then move the borer elsewhere a little later, and do this all around. Then use chisels to cut away the space between the perforations, doing this most skillfully and gently, as we have said, until you can pull out the bone with your hand or with one of the tools you have, like tweezers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and make sure you do not touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone and made an incision, it is appropriate that you resect the membrane which is attached to the bone with some other tool resembling a scalpel, but it should be more delicate and thinner than the other scalpel;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if it is sticking to any small bones or any scales, gently remove them with the instrument;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound as we have described earlier.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	Another method of treatment which is safer, according to Galen, is as follows:
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and he praises it highly, and it is his word we are quoting.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture is open and moving; then, when you have uncovered that part, place underneath it the head of this lens-shaped instrument, which has a curved shape.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And it does not cut from one side only but has a dual cutting edge, so that the blade is facing the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike gently with a small hammer all around the bone, taking care not to hit the membrane underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is attached to the bone, gently loosen it, because bones can be loosened without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not go all the way through to the membrane, and the bone is only cut slightly on top, with small pieces, then you should re-examine that roughness, and remove the scales with a sharp rasp, of which you must have several quantities, to use in each place the most suitable one according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	First use the coarse rasps, then the finer ones, and do not stop until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	For each of the other hairline fractures and subtle breaks, you should treat them according to their location;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is not something that can be learned by someone who has dedicated themselves to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the sinus is exposed, you should dampen a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, moisten it in rose oil, and place it over the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled over two or three times, moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as gently as you can so that you do not burden the ulcer, then apply it above with another piece of linen and do not pull tighter than it holds the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it like that for a day or two until the abscesses are soothed, then remove it and apply remedies such as roots of lilies, and flour of beans, and incense powder, and aristology, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and make a powder from these things and put it on the wound, then apply remedies from moon-worshippers without biting;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and watch that the wound is clean so that you do not leave any of the ointment or any dirt on it, for when dirt gathers on the brain's membrane and hardens, great harm comes to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one applies something biting to an ulcer, it bites from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if discoloration does not go away except through the medicine that one has put on it, because of its power, you must take a part of honey, and three parts rose oil, and apply it to the ulcer.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal it in the way that is appropriate, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes both sides of the jaw are broken, or just one side, because there are two bones. If both sides are broken, they can be reset with a splint so they heal straight and even; if only one is broken, it must be set by itself, as will now be described.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	The lower part is cartilaginous and does not break unless forced or twisted, then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must put your little finger or a tool into the jaw, and place the break inside your index finger, and hold it steady with your thumb, until the jaw returns to its natural shape. This may take several days.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and be sure that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is above the elbow and the bone cannot be put in place, then you should place it evenly at the top of a fairly thick rod.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if there is a fracture in two parts, do the same, and be quick to restore the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses are healed, then put on the top of the fracture tenting with linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you put the other one elsewhere, if there is a fracture there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the tents be so thick that they fill the holes of the bone.Et li chief dou neis est si conme une gie de fer, ou une piece d’armure, ou
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one must wet the bandages with butter, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	And the top of the bone is like a piece of iron or armor, or it does not seem to me that this is good, but it should be moistened with egg white and flour ground fine;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then let the tent remain, until the bone is set, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes they put in goose feathers instead of tents, and around it a thin cloth, and the break is held, and the patient breathes through it;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or do what you want.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if there are abscesses on the nose while you are doing this, put cerotic ointment or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a pouch of diaquilone.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if a boil comes, put on a plaster made of flour of wheat bran, and incense powder, cooked with egg white, then put on light tow, but do not tie it tightly;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the fracture of the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it with appropriate instruments, then cut the wound, and treat it with warm things, healing, as with plasters and ointments appropriate to such;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound within the nose, then treat it with tents, and put in splints of lead, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the dislocation of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fully dislocated and there is no external wound, and only the joint is dislocated, not broken in two where the corbel sits inside, then it is easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	If the fracture is on the right side, you must place your index finger into the mouth of the patient.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is in the left jaw, then insert your index finger from your right hand and gently push into the fracture and ease it with the other hand, making sure it is even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the joint of the jaw is displaced to one side, you should administer an extension of one part, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if there is movement of the teeth, or a fracture, then they should be restrained with a wire of gold or silver or silk, then place cerate on the broken jaw and over it a double drape.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And place upon the drape a heavy, well-made stele or a piece of leather the same size, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it on as tightly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that it is changing shape, then loosen it on the third day, and then reset it to its proper position.Et si tu dises que li membres sont trop tiens, si deslie la nuit, et le matien remise a point, et comande a malaide qu’il ne se mueze point tant qu’il soit
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply a poultice made of powdered eggs or flour mixed with water after removing the cerote.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and if the poultice doesn't help and the condition of the patient doesn't improve, leave it until the wound heals.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	often, it heals within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses come, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine whether any piece of bone has been dislodged;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	and remove it with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flames according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, then close the wound, if it is wide, and place upon it suitable poultices to promote healing, until it is cured.
de la forcele	of the foreskin
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The fracture often occurs in front of the shoulder in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	one where it is broken and dislocated in two places, with pieces, and is the easiest to heal;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or one where there is a break with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the procedure is when the fracture does not have an open wound: you need two assistants so that one can hold the shoulder where the fracture is;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the others stretch their necks towards the wound;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then even out the fracture with your fingers so that it is smooth and has no bumps or bumps.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend further, place a round piece of cloth or woolen cloth under the patient's shoulder, as thick as necessary;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and gently pull on the collarbone, while pressing the round piece of cloth with your hand to smooth out the fracture, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder out of joint because it is dislocated, then the patient should lie on his back, and place under the shoulder a small pillow, and the assistant should press the shoulder down, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	Then gently feel the fracture with your fingers, and if you find it broken, you must split it open;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined due to any protrusion, then cut it off at one of the incisions you made;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but place this instrument under the collarbone to protect the windpipe:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and resembles a spoon, and is not sharp-edged, and is as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it has two heads, as you can see, and one is wide and the other narrow, as is the opening of the wound that you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are sure of a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the opening is small, or if you doubt about a hot abscess, dress the wound with bandages and poultices, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes out, moisten a bandage in rose oil and garlic and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The dislocation of the bone, when there is no wound or incision, is to put on the bone the plaster made from mill-dust and egg white, and place light bandages over it, and put a pillow under the shoulder, if necessary;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	take a very large bandage, one palm wide, then place double draping over sponges, and anoint it;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	take a thin board three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs down;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	place the board over the break, and wrap the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the sick armpit;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and reset it from each side, and when you see that the limb holds the break correctly, and you see clearly that the board does not move over the broken bone, then release it every day, and when the ligature slackens, restrain it again;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his back, and when he sleeps, place a small pillow under the armpit to lift the shoulder up;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if you ease the dislocation of the shoulder by aligning it, or tie his arm to his neck, and do not untie him if no evil accident happens until 20 days have passed;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then begin the poultice again if you see that he still needs it, and keep doing this until he is healed;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and she is healed within 28 days in some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It can happen that the shoulder dislocates or breaks suddenly without any violence, and is not known until it is touched;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	then you should set it according to the shape of the dislocation, and reset it in every way you can according to its natural form;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then place powder from the mill with egg white, and light bandages, and over this a double layer of cloth;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then place a wide and thin pillow on top, slightly wider than the shoulder, and if there is a indentation beneath the pillow anywhere on the shoulder, fill that indentation with a wad of linen, so that the pillow lies flat.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	then tightly bind it all with a large bandage, so that the pillow doesn't move from its place, and check the binding every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and whenever it softens, bind it tightly again and put the pillow back in its place if it has moved out of position, and let the patient lie on his side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	The shoulder is restored within 20 or 25 days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number of days is complete, then loosen it, and be sure, for it isn't an easy thing for the bone to move back into place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward and not underneath the heart, pierce and open the bone, and do what we have said about the fracture of the collarbone to soothe the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bone in the middle sometimes gets broken, but that happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks apart during treatment.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	When it is broken in the middle, it inclines downward, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks strength, and becomes dizzy, and sometimes vomits blood, and the hair falls out from the broken bone, and he feels much better.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back, and he puts a pillow between his shoulders, then presses his shoulders, and brings together the sides of the two ribs with his hands, and carefully aligns them equally in all ways that he can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then he applies poultices and compresses made of linen onto the broken bone, using a subtle amount of salt or other light material, and wraps it in a cloth, tying it onto the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	then he turns the ligament around to the back, and tightens it gently, and checks every hour how loose it is, and if it softens, then he tightens it;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it needs to be loosened due to corrosion or itching that has come to the area, or pain or an abscess, then be quick and loosen it, remove the poultice, and address what has come about in ways of treatment;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reset the dislocation and hold it until it heals.
de la brisure des costes	about the breaking of ribs:
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	You should know that rib fractures only occur in the large ribs near the back, and in the front, and they only bend because they are slippery.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and the patient feels pain in the area as you press.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you reset the break as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the ointment and bind it with a bandage, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the rib fracture is inward-sloping, the patient feels great pain and a piercing sensation, as with pneumonia, because the bone punctures the lung.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and it hurts when pressed, and the patient feels shortness of breath and vomits a great quantity of blood, which is a serious illness, and the ancients considered it dangerous.
